**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Firefox CSS calc() Value Overflow

## Your Task

Firefox crashes when processing CSS calc() with extreme values. Find the C++ source files in mozilla/gecko-dev that (1) parse CSS calc() expressions and (2) handle numeric overflow during calc() value resolution.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the incident domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/firefox--871325b8.

492026-03-08T21:06:31.838051agentmessage-
I am thinking...: Now I have a clearer picture. The key files for CSS calc() parsing and overflow handling in Firefox are:

1. **Parsing CSS calc() expressions:**
   - `servo/components/style/values/specified/calc.rs` - The main Rust file that parses CSS calc() expressions. It defines `MathFunction`, `Leaf`, and `CalcNode` types, and implements the parsing logic.
   - `servo/components/style/values/generics/calc.rs` - The generic calc node implementation that defines `GenericCalcNode`, `CalcNodeLeaf`, `CalcUnits`, etc.
   - `servo/components/style/values/computed/length_percentage.rs` - The computed value representation for calc() with length-percentage values, including the `CalcLengthPercentage` struct with `clamping_mode`.

- `layout/style/ServoCSSParser.cpp` - C++ wrapper that delegates to Servo's `Servo_ParseProperty` for all CSS parsing including calc()

## C++ Files for CSS calc() Parsing

Firefox uses Servo (Rust) for CSS parsing. The C++ side of calc() parsing is handled through:

1. **`layout/style/ServoCSSParser.cpp`** - C++ wrapper that delegates all CSS property parsing (including calc()) to Servo via `Servo_ParseProperty`. This is the entry point for C++ code to parse CSS values.

2. **`layout/style/ServoStyleConstsInlines.h`** - C++ inline implementations for calc() value resolution:
   - `StyleCalcLengthPercentage::Resolve(nscoord aBasis, Rounder aRounder)` - resolves a calc() expression to an nscoord, applying a rounding function
   - `LengthPercentage::Resolve(...)` - multiple overloads that resolve LengthPercentage (which can be a calc() expression) to nscoord
   - `LengthPercentage::ScaleLengthsBy(float aScale)` - scales length values in a calc() expression
   - `LengthPercentage::ResolveToCSSPixels(CSSCoord aPercentageBasis)` - resolves to CSS pixels

3. **`layout/style/nsStyleStruct.cpp`** - Implements `StyleCalcNode::ScaleLengthsBy(float aScale)` - a C++ template specialization that traverses the calc() AST (Leaf, Clamp, Round, ModRem, MinMax, Sum, Product nodes) and scales all length values.

## C++ Files for Numeric Overflow During calc() Value Resolution

1. **`gfx/src/nsCoord.h`** - The core overflow-handling header for CSS coordinate values:
   - `NSToCoordRoundWithClamp(float/double)` - bounds-checks before converting float to nscoord, clamping to nscoord_MAX/nscoord_MIN
   - `NSToCoordFloorClamped(float)` - floor with overflow clamping
   - `NSToCoordCeilClamped(double)` - ceil with overflow clamping
   - `NSCoordSaturatingAdd(nscoord a, nscoord b)` - saturating addition capping at nscoord_MAX
   - `NSCoordSatura

732026-03-08T21:10:07.793329agentmessage-
The answer has been written to `/workspace/answer.json`. Here is a structured summary of the findings:

---

## Findings

### (1) C++ Files That Parse CSS calc() Expressions

Firefox moved CSS parsing entirely to Servo (Rust). The C++ side participates through three files:

| File | Role |
|---|---|
| `layout/style/ServoCSSParser.cpp` | Thin C++ wrapper; `ParseProperty()` delegates to `Servo_ParseProperty()` (Rust FFI). No calc-specific C++ parsing logic. |
| `layout/style/ServoStyleConstsInlines.h` | Inline C++ templates that **resolve** the Rust-generated calc AST to `nscoord`. `LengthPercentage::Resolve()` calls `AsCalc().Resolve(basis, rounder)` when the value is a calc node. Also provides `ScaleLengthsBy()`. |
| `layout/style/nsStyleStruct.cpp` | Implements `template<> void StyleCalcNode::ScaleLengthsBy(float)` — the only C++ function that directly traverses the calc AST (Leaf, Clamp, Round, ModRem, MinMax, Sum, Product nodes). |

The actual parsing lives in Rust:
- `servo/components/style/values/specified/calc.rs` — `MathFunction` enum, `Leaf` enum, `CalcNode::parse()` / `parse_one()`; stores `clamping_mode: AllowedNumericType`
- `servo/components/style/values/generics/calc.rs` — `GenericCalcNode<L>`, `CalcNodeLeaf` trait, `CalcUnits`, `RoundingStrategy`
- `servo/components/style/values/computed/length_percentage.rs` — `CalcLengthPercentage::resolve()` applies `clamping_mode.clamp()`

---

### (2) C++ Files That Handle Numeric Overflow During calc() Value Resolution

| File | Mechanism |
|---|---|
| **`gfx/src/nsCoord.h`** | Core overflow library. `NSToCoordRoundWithClamp()` bounds-checks floats before converting to `nscoord` (capped at `nscoord_MAX = (1<<30)-1`). `NSCoordSaturatingAdd/Subtract/Multiply()` implement saturating arithmetic. Used everywhere a calc() 
... (truncated)

`LengthPercentage::ScaleLengthsBy(float aScale)` - scales length values in a calc() expression\n   - `LengthPercentage::ResolveToCSSPixels(CSSCoord aPercentageBasis)` - resolves to CSS pixels\n\n3. **`layout/style/nsStyleStruct.cpp`** - Implements `StyleCalcNode::ScaleLengthsBy(float aScale)` - a C++ template specialization that traverses the calc() AST (Leaf, Clamp, Round, ModRem, MinMax, Sum, Product nodes) and scales all length values.\n\n## C++ Files for Numeric Overflow During calc() Value Resolution\n\n1. **`gfx/src/nsCoord.h`** - `NSToCoordFloorClamped(float)` - floor with overflow clamping\n   - `NSToCoordCeilClamped(double)` - ceil with overflow clamping\n   - `NSCoordSaturatingAdd(nscoord a, nscoord b)` - saturating addition capping at nscoord_MAX\n   - internal helper\n\n2. **`dom/svg/SVGContentUtils.cpp`** - `SVGContentUtils::CoordToFloat()` (lines 873-889):\n   - Resolves a `LengthPercentage` (which can be a calc() expression) to a float\n   - Explicitly checks `calc.clamping_mode == StyleAllowedNumericType::NonNegative` and clamps the result to 0 if negative\n   - This is direct C++ overflow/clamping handling for calc() values\n\n3. **`layout/style/nsComputedDOMStyle.cpp`** - `nsComputedDOMStyle::SetValueToLengthPercentage()` (lines 2187-2208):\n   - Takes a `bool aClampNegativeCalc` parameter\n   -
